<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF Identification (RFID) has become mainstream and its various applications can be found in many industries ranging from defense to healthcare, from customer to enterprise, and from supply chain to value chain. Since the RFID reader is a radio transceiver, which works as transmitter and receiver to communicate with a tag, it faces the same challenges as all radios encounter, as well as a few specialized problems unusual in wireless communications. The RFID reader communicating with a passive or semipassive tag must operate in full-duplex mode such that it must transmit continuous wave (CW) in order for the tag to backscatter while listening to the tag response. However, since the tag signal is essentially at the same frequency as the reader's own signal, a duplexer cannot be used to remove the transmitted signal. Hence, the leakage from the transmitter to the receiver can be an important limit in the receiver sensitivity.</p><p>Conventional RFID readers are typically designed with general approaches to minimize the leakage, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> (<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>). In these structures, the receiver input will be exposed to a substantial signal from the transmitter due to the reflection from the antenna and the limitation of the isolation performance of the components such as the circulator, directional coupler, or hybrid coupler. A commercial circulator, directional coupler, or hybrid coupler generally provides about 25 dB of isolation characteristic in the well-matched condition. If the antenna and transceiver are not well matched, the Tx leakage will be increased. In the conventional structures, the Tx leakage is critically affected by the antenna impedance variation and is not quite sufficient for guaranteed receiver sensitivity and reading range. In the RFID reader, the performance of the antenna is also important in order to extract information from the weak signal backscattered by the tag and provide affluent power to the tag. Antennas for the RFID reader in most cases have circular polarization (CP) to avoid potential strong polarization losses due to a linear polarization of the transponder antenna oriented arbitrarily. In addition, the radiation pattern of the antenna should be suitable to achieve the appropriate readable range for a given application. Recently, patch and helix (spiral) antennas are used widely because of their excellent CP and high gain characteristics (<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Conventional RFID front-end for isolation between Tx and Rx by using: (a) a circulator, (b) a directional coupler, (c) a quadrature hybrid, and (d) two antennas.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811950/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In this paper, we propose a new front-end structure for the ultra-high-frequency (UHF) RFID reader, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>. The proposed front-end structure consists of the balanced directional coupler and four-port feed antenna. The proposed front-end structure has high and robust Tx leakage cancellation characteristic regardless of the antenna load variation and mutual coupling.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Balanced Directional Coupler</h2></div><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig><p>Proposed balanced front-end system with high isolation between Tx and Rx.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811950/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Conventional directional coupler with mismatched load. overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -3.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 6.737em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-20">\eqalign{s_{11}=&amp;\,T^{2}\left(\alpha_{A}^{2}\Gamma_{A}-\alpha_{B}^{2}\Gamma_{B}\right)\cr s_{12}=&amp;\,TC(\alpha_{A}\Gamma_{A}-\alpha_{B}\Gamma_{B})+I(\alpha_{A}-\alpha_{B})\cr s_{21}=&amp;\,TC(\alpha_{A}\Gamma_{A}-\alpha_{B}\Gamma_{B})+I(\alpha_{A}-\alpha_{B})\cr s_{22}=&amp;\,C^{2}(\Gamma_{A}-\Gamma_{B}).}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalign{s_{11}=&amp;\,T^{2}\left(\alpha_{A}^{2}\Gamma_{A}-\alpha_{B}^{2}\Gamma_{B}\right)\cr s_{12}=&amp;\,TC(\alpha_{A}\Gamma_{A}-\alpha_{B}\Gamma_{B})+I(\alpha_{A}-\alpha_{B})\cr s_{21}=&amp;\,TC(\alpha_{A}\Gamma_{A}-\alpha_{B}\Gamma_{B})+I(\alpha_{A}-\alpha_{B})\cr s_{22}=&amp;\,C^{2}(\Gamma_{A}-\Gamma_{B}).}</span></span></disp-formula>

font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">B</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-861" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-862" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-863" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">(\alpha_{A}=\alpha_{B}=1)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is noted that the proposed structure shows the isolation characteristics, which are robust for varying load impedance and path loss, and relatively better than that of a single directional coupler.</p></div>

<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> discussed the isolation characteristics of the balanced coupler structure with no mutual coupling assumed between two antenna ports. In this section, we will continue the Tx leakage analysis on the coupling effect on the proposed structure.<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. <p></p><p>Therefore, considerations on minimizing the coupling between antenna ports will be essential to improve the isolation features of the balanced coupler.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Four-Port Feed Antenna</h3><p>We propose the four-port antenna structure for which the antenna coupling effect is minimized. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>, the ports are located along the dotted circle where two adjacent points have 90Â° of interval from each other. <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Experimental Results</h2></div><p>The proposed front-end structure is implemented by two parts: the balanced directional coupler and four-port feed antenna. To verify the validity of the proposed structure, various measurements about the front-end features are performed. First, the isolation characteristic of the balanced directional coupler in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> is measured for load variation. Subsequently, the isolation characteristic of the balanced directional coupler with the four-port feed antenna in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a> is tested. Finally, we measure the radiation characteristic of the proposed four-port antennas.</p><p>The balanced directional coupler feeder has been fabricated on a 0.5-mm-thick Taconic substrate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1978" role="math" style="width: 4.748em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.267em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1979"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1980" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1981"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1982" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Îµ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1983"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1984"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1985" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1986" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1987" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">3.5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1988" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">(\varepsilon_{r}=3.5)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For the quadrature hybrid branch line coupler and 10-dB directional coupler, commercial low-temperature co-fired ceramic (LTCC) components, RCP890A03 and RCP890A10, are employed, respectively.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Balanced Directional Coupler</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a> shows the test environment for load variation of the balanced directional coupler. Various antenna loads <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1989" role="math" style="width: 3.547em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.186em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.07em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1990"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1991" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1992"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1993" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1994"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1995"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1996" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">A</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1997" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">N</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1998" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1999" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">(R_{\rm ANT})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which represent the matching condition of the antenna, are connected to two antenna ports. The measured results of the isolation characteristic for the single contra-directional coupler in varying load impedance condition (25, 50, 75, and 100 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2000" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2001"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2002" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11(a)</a>. In a perfectly matched case (50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2003" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2004"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2005" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), about 38.9 dB of isolation is obtained at 910 MHz. For the other load impedances, the isolation is measured from 22.1 to 25.4 dB. The identical test is applied to the proposed balanced directional coupler. The measured results of the isolation characteristic for the proposed structure across the industrialâscientificâmedical (ISM) UHF RFID frequency band are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11(b)</a>. In a perfectly matched case (50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2006" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2007"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2008" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), the isolation feature is measured about 62.1 dB at 910 MHz. The proposed structure also provides 45.4 dB of isolation for 100 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2009" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2012" role="math" style="width: 7.631em; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-2017" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-2018" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">9.54</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-2019" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2020"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2021"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-2022"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2023"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-2024" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-2025" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; It is verified that the proposed balanced structure has quite robust isolation characteristics for load impedance variation.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Balanced Directional Coupler With Four Inverted-F Antennas</h3><p>

<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a> shows the balanced directional coupler with four inverted-F antennas. Four inverted-F antennas are printed on an FR4 substrate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2026" role="math" style="width: 4.748em; <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a> shows the measured radiation pattern at 910MHz. The proposed structure has a right-hand circular polarization (RHCP) characteristic, a peak gain of 3.9 dBic, and half-power beamwidth (HPBW) corresponding to about 135Â°. It also has approximately a 1.5-dB axial ratio at the measured frequency.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Balanced Directional Coupler With Four-Port Feed Patch Antenna</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a> shows the balanced directional coupler with a four-port feed patch antenna. The four-port feed patch antenna is printed on an FR4 substrate with 0.6-mm thickness. The width of the antenna is 130 mm and the height is 15 mm. The balanced directional coupler is printed on an FR4 substrate with 0.5-mm thickness and a size of 80 mm Ã 62 mm and is attached to the ground plane with the size of 190 mm Ã 190 mm. The isolation characteristic of the balanced directional coupler with a four-port feed patch antenna is measured as 50 dB in the UHF RFID band, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 16</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17</a> shows the measured radiation pattern of a four-port feed patch antenna at 910 MHz. The proposed structure has an RHCP characteristic, a peak gain of 8.05 dBic, and a HPBW corresponding to about 130Â°. It also has approximately a 1.0-dB axial ratio at the measured frequency.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 15. </b><fig><p>Fabricated balanced directional coupler with four-port patch antenna. <div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811950/4811950-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 16. </b><fig><p>Measured isolation characteristic of the balanced directional coupler with four-port patch antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811950/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>An RFID reader front-end with Tx leakage cancellation has been studied. The isolation characteristics of the balanced directional coupler circuit were verified by numerical analysis and measurements. Additionally, the balanced directional coupler with a four-port feed antenna was proposed. The proposed front-end structure provided 45â50 dB of isolation between the transmitter and receiver.</p></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
